Unprecedented Bumper Harvest in Decades 130

Jiangsu Province May Have a Surplus of Six or Seven Million Shi

Next Year's Food Supply for the People is Expected to Be Worry-Free

The Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday presented a report to the National Government and the Executive Yuan, stating that the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Pan Gongzhan, had forwarded a report from the Food Committee. After hearing the news of the bumper autumn harvest, the Committee instructed representatives of the food industry and various committee members to conduct investigations at any time for reference. According to the report from the food industry committee, all producing areas have reported a bumper harvest this year. In Jiangsu Province, areas that usually yield less than two shi per mu can yield three shi this year. Areas north of the Yangtze River that usually grow miscellaneous grains have also switched to rice cultivation this year. The situation in northern Huaihe is the same. Currently, the best japonica rice in Shanghai sells for 15-16 yuan per shi, which is 5-6 yuan lower than during the lean season this year, and there is still potential for further decline. Dujian rice sells for only a little over 10 yuan. Jiangxi indica rice sells for only 10.2 yuan per dan. One dan of milled white rice, which weighs 224 jin, costs only 5 yuan. Anhui rice production costs at most 8 yuan, and Hunan rice costs only 6 yuan. Furthermore, areas such as Si'an and Jiashan are blocked and have no place to sell their produce. Tianjin also had a good early rice harvest, which is estimated to be one million dan higher than in previous years. It is estimated that Jiangsu Province may have a surplus of six or seven million shi of rice. In addition, several rice ears were sent for inspection, and the largest ear had up to 209 grains, and the next largest had 170 grains. In addition to instructing them to continue investigating in the producing areas of Jiangsu, Anhui, Hunan, and Jiangxi, it is believed that the committee members' reports are based on communications from firms in the producing areas and cannot be considered entirely accurate. However, based on rice prices and the rice ears sent for inspection, it is estimated that what they say is not entirely false. In ordinary years, a rice ear usually has 120-130 grains, and it is rare to see more than 140 grains. This year, the number of grains is not only more than that, but also up to 200 or more, which is a good omen. Because agricultural affairs in our country are not well-developed, the harvest depends entirely on the weather. It cannot be compared to farmland that uses scientific methods, where each ear can have 240 grains. At a time when the forces of warlords have been cleared and the overall situation of unification has been completed, it is even more gratifying to have this unprecedented bumper harvest in decades. It is appropriate to submit this report along with photos of the auspicious grains to the Municipal Government and the Executive Yuan of the National Government for review and implementation for the convenience of the public. Based on this, the report that the autumn harvest is the best in decades and that the people's strength is reviving is gratifying. In addition to submitting the report and issuing instructions, it is appropriate to submit one photo of the auspicious grains along with this report for your review and for the convenience of the public.

Provincial Order Still Favors Deferring Repayment of Borrowed Grain Transport 131

The Shanghai County Government recently received a report from Wu, the chief of the first district, stating that 4.5 yuan per shi is still owed for the advance borrowing of winter grain transport. According to previous orders, 9 jiao per shi should be repaid from the 19th year until it is cleared in the 23rd year. Therefore, a request was made to retract the order to defer repayment to alleviate the people's difficulties. The county government forwarded the request to the Jiangsu Department of Finance for review. The department ordered, "The advance borrowing of winter grain transport was approved by the Provincial Government Committee, and the deferral of repayment was originally intended to address the provincial budget deficit and provide relief. It should be understood by those who are concerned and love the country. The request to retract the order concerns a general issue and cannot be approved." County Magistrate Yan issued an order yesterday, instructing the township and town chiefs of the district to comply with the order.

Discussion on the Retention or Abolition of the Five-County Joint Defense 132

The five counties of Shanghai, Songjiang, Nanqiao, Fengxian, and Qingpu have convened multiple meetings regarding joint defense at Shangmei and Songjiang. The date for the current regular meeting was set for November 30th, and it was supposed to be convened by the Nanhui County Government. However, the Shanghai County Government received a letter from County Magistrate Kong of Nanhui stating that the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs has already made separate provisions for the division of county joint defenses. The letter asks if the five-county joint defense should continue to meet or be temporarily suspended. After receiving the letter, County Magistrate Yan believed that it was appropriate to convene the current meeting of the joint defense for discussion and decision. Therefore, he sent a letter to Nanhui County for their reference.

Director Yuan Plans Winter Defense 133

Dispatching New Police to Assist in Protection

Negotiating Joint Defense with the Concessions

Recently, Yuan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, considering the arrival of winter and the unrest caused by bandits, has been making winter defense a priority. All defense measures were thoroughly discussed at the previous bureau meeting with the heads of various districts and teams. Several winter defense measures were formulated and circulated to all districts and teams for compliance. As the implementation date approaches and the jurisdiction is vast, bordering the concessions in all directions, the police force is thin and insufficient for deployment. Director Yuan has specially instructed the newly expanded Sixth Police Company Commander to supervise the newly recruited police officers (i.e., the police recruits who graduated from this year's police training school) to intensify their training in preparation for dispatch to assist in defense in various districts in the north and south. Regarding the issue of joint defense between the Chinese and concession territories, personnel have been dispatched to negotiate with the British and French Concession police chiefs and inspectors. In the event of bandit alarms, they will cooperate regardless of jurisdictional boundaries to prevent hiding and avoid conflicts.

Silk Factories Submit Urgent Request for Public Bonds

To Survive the End of the Year and Avoid Bankruptcy 134

Shanghai silk factories, due to the slump in European sales of white filature silk, have suffered substantial financial losses and are unable to sustain operations. A general meeting was held to elect representatives to go to the capital to petition for the issuance of 10 million yuan in public bonds for the silk industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai, along with representatives from Zhejiang and Wuxi who were temporarily added. The petition results were quite satisfactory. The Executive Yuan agreed to instruct the relevant ministries to deliberate, and the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry also agreed to make every effort to maintain the industry. It has been learned that the petition representatives returned to Shanghai half a month ago, and some silk factories have already resumed operations with encouragement to maintain the livelihood of workers. However, due to the lack of funding and the increasingly sluggish overseas silk sales, the financial community is wary of offering loans against dry cocoons due to concerns about labor unrest, and they dare not hand them over to factories for reeling. The work remains difficult to sustain. Moreover, with the end of the year approaching, silk cocoon pledges cannot be repaid, and bankruptcy is imminent. Recently, the owners of various silk factories have approached Shen Huachen, Chairman of the Silk Industry Association, requesting him to find a way to submit an urgent request to the Executive Yuan to issue public bonds within the year to survive the end of the year and avoid bankruptcy.

Zhejiang Provincial Association Pleads for Silk Merchants 135

Telegram to Chairman Chiang

Requesting Exemption from Silk Cocoon Tax

The Zhejiang Provincial Association telegraphed Chairman Chiang on behalf of silk cocoon merchants: "To His Excellency Chairman Chiang of the National Government: Since the cessation of European sales of Chinese silk, merchants have suspended their business, workers have lost their jobs, and the dry cocoon raw materials in the interior, due to the stagnant silk market, cannot find buyers even at reduced prices. Therefore, those who were once considered well-off in the silk cocoon industry will soon become impoverished. The current decline in the silk market only affects the silk cocoon merchants and the male and female workers associated with the silk factories. If this continues without remedy, the farmers in the dry cocoon raw material producing areas will suffer the most. Zhejiang is the most prosperous region for sericulture, producing millions of piculs of cocoons each year. The influx of foreign capital is substantial, and the general population relies on this to pay rent, taxes, and support their families. Once this source of income is cut off, the livelihoods of farmers will be in dire straits. If we revert to reeling native silk, the various silk weaving factories that are now barely surviving will be oversupplied, and they will not be able to absorb the excess. Fertile sericultural land will turn into barren land, and we are deeply apprehensive about the future. The reason for the decline of Chinese silk is the pressure from Japanese silk, which is selling at discounted prices. Japanese silk is backed by government subsidies, so it can continue to lower prices without harming individual businesses. The cost of Chinese silk is higher, and the commercial strength is weaker. Selling at discounted prices will lead to bankruptcy, resulting in the current stalemate. Therefore, the only way to remedy Chinese silk is to find ways to reduce costs. We propose that Your Excellency, mindful of the importance of sericulture to the livelihoods of the people in the southeast, instruct the Ministry of Finance to carefully review and deliberate, and order all customs bureaus to exempt all taxes and levies on raw silk exports and on dry cocoons, so that the future of silk cocoons may be improved. If the cocoon tax is exempted, the cost of raw materials will be lower; if the export tax is exempted, the cost will be even lower, and the price will be even lower. Merchants, appreciating the government's willingness to sacrifice national funds, will strive to improve the quality of their products. If this is done, Chinese silk can still compete with Japanese silk. Otherwise, the irreversible phenomenon will be difficult to reverse, and the European and American markets may no longer see Chinese silk. However, given the current inadequate national finances, the silk cocoon tax revenue is a significant source of government revenue, and a sudden request for exemption may seem alarming. We are aware that silk and tea are treated equally and are major Chinese exports. The government, mindful of the tea industry's failure in recent years, has reduced or exempted tea export taxes for four years. As machine-made foreign goods are already exempt from taxes under the Ministry of Finance's explicit order, it seems not excessive to request that raw silk, also a machine-made product, be granted the same exemption. Fortunately, customs autonomy, tariff reduction, and tax increases are imminent, and the opportunity can be used to revise the tariff schedule and appropriately increase import taxes to offset the loss. The various artificial silks, silk fabrics, wool fabrics, etc. imported from various countries are all enemies that plunder our country's silk industry, and their imports have been increasing year by year. If the tariffs are specially increased to offset the silk cocoon tax revenue, there should be no fear of insufficient national revenue. This is a well-rounded plan that takes both commercial sentiment and national interests into account and can protect domestic production. Currently, with the closure of all silk factories in Shanghai, the association has telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce requesting a reduction or exemption of the silk cocoon tax and has proposed both fundamental and temporary solutions to help alleviate the crisis. Now that the crisis of silk cocoons is becoming more urgent and the dangers of sericulture are surrounding us, the association, as a collective organization of Zhejiang people in Shanghai, is deeply concerned about our homeland and spares no effort to speak out repeatedly on behalf of the tens of millions of farmers in Zhejiang. This is not only to seek relief for silk cocoons, but also because silk cocoons are an important national product of our country, and agriculture, industry, and commerce are all directly related. Saving merchants is saving workers and also saving farmers. At a time when the whole country is eagerly looking forward to good governance, we urgently appeal to Your Excellency to implement these measures. We are submitting this urgent telegram in the hope that you will take note. Zhejiang Provincial Association prostrates itself."

Bamboo Industry Federation Strives for Tax Laws 136

The Jiangsu Provincial Bamboo Tax Rate was previously requested by the Jiangsu-Shanghai-Changshu Bamboo Industry Federation to the Finance Bureau for approval. The tax rate for moso bamboo was 1.6 yuan per post, while other light bamboo, bundle bamboo, thin bamboo, bamboo poles, and various utensils were exempted from taxation. The federation notified all colleagues to comply with the payment of taxes. Recently, it was heard that the Wuxi Special Tax Bureau had included light, thin bundle bamboo in the assessment for miscellaneous bamboo taxation. The colleagues in Wuxi reported this to the association. As a result, a meeting was convened to discuss the matter. It was unanimously believed that the Wuxi Special Tax Bureau was clearly defying the law, affecting the industry. Therefore, a notice was printed and sent to all raft owners yesterday stating that if the above situation occurs, they can immediately report to the federation, which will be responsible for negotiating. Subsequently, the name of the association was changed to "Jiangsu-Shanghai-Changshu-Yukun-Wuxi" Bamboo Industry Federation to strengthen the unity of the organization.

Foreign Merchants' Insurance Association Accepts Stamp Duty 137

Chinese Insurance Policies Prepared for Actual Stamping

Sales Representatives to Discuss Procedures Regularly

Since the Shanghai Bureau of the Jiangsu Provincial Stamp Tax of the Ministry of Finance launched the promotion of stamp duty in special zones, the results have been excellent. The insurance industry has specially appointed Mr. Wang Yanxiang to be responsible for the promotion of stamp duty. An office has been set up at No. 372 Minyong Lane, Nanjing Road, in the Public Concession, and preparations are well underway. The Chinese insurance industry has already complied with the regulations and actually stamped the policies. However, due to the restrictions of unequal treaties on the foreign merchants' side, negotiations have been held several times. Recently, the Consular Corps has acknowledged that all Chinese insurance policies should be stamped in accordance with the regulations. However, fearing that it would be difficult to understand at the beginning, Mr. Wang, a sales representative of the Bureau's insurance industry, has scheduled a tea party at the Atlantic Restaurant at 3:00 p.m. on the 26th to invite Chinese managers of various foreign insurance companies to discuss all stamping procedures.

Fifty representatives from various circles attended. Chairman Zhu Shiqi was elected to preside over the meeting as scheduled. The chairman reported on the implementation of the resolutions of the previous meeting. Subsequently, Xu Yefu reported on the details of the negotiations with the French authorities, and the goals of punishing the culprit, apology, and compensation were all achieved. Ding and Huang personally stated to the representatives from all walks of life that they were very satisfied with the results of the negotiations and expressed their gratitude. Finally, it was resolved that the association would send letters of thanks to Mr. Chen Yi, a standing committee member of the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association and the Municipal Public Training Association, and to Mr. Xu Yefu and Mr. Zhu Shiqi. It was also heard that, in order to prevent future troubles, the various circles in Xuhui decided to submit a serious request to the diplomatic authorities for the withdrawal of the French sailors stationed beyond the border, and that they would strive to publicize the issue until the sailors were withdrawn.

Jiangsu High Court Recruits Trial Judges 142

Jiangsu High Court Announcement No. 52: For the purpose of announcement, the court is currently holding a trial judge examination. The revised examination regulations have been submitted to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for consultation and approval by the Examination Committee. Registration is scheduled to begin on November 24, 19, and close on January 6, 20. The examination will begin on January 19, 20. Those who meet the qualifications and wish to apply should follow the articles of the regulations and register at the Trial Judge Examination Affairs Office of the court within the registration period. They should pay a registration fee of 2 yuan and obtain a resume and guarantee form to fill out according to the prescribed format. They should also attach a recent 4-inch half-length photograph and submit the qualification documents to the court for review before January 6, 20. Do not delay. This announcement is hereby made. Attached is an excerpt of the regulations. President Lin Biao, November 20, Republic of China, Year 19.

Excerpt of the revised provisional regulations for the Jiangsu County Trial Judge Examination: Article 4: Anyone who is 20 years old or older and possesses one of the following qualifications may apply for the Jiangsu County Trial Judge Examination: (1) Graduated from a national, public, or approved private university or specialized school with a degree in law or political science. (2) Graduated from a foreign university or specialized school with a degree in law or political science. (3) Possesses qualifications equivalent to an appointed position and has handled judicial or administrative affairs for more than two years. Article 5: Even if one possesses the qualifications in the preceding article, one may not apply for the Jiangsu County Trial Judge Examination if one has any of the following: (1) Engaged in counter-revolutionary activities. (2) Been sentenced to imprisonment. (3) Been deprived of civil rights or suspended from civil rights and has not yet been restored. (4) Is of base character and has been accused of a case that has been verified. (5) Has been declared bankrupt and has not yet been restored. (6) Has a mental illness or is physically weak. (7) Is in arrears of public funds or has embezzled public funds. (8) Other laws have special provisions. Article 6: The examination is divided into three stages: the first, second, and third examinations. The first and second examinations are written, while the third examination is oral. Only those who pass the first examination may take the second examination, and only those who pass the second examination may take the third examination. Article 7: The subjects for the first examination are as follows: (1) Party Ideology and Program (2) Chinese Language (3) General Theory of Law. Article 8: The subjects for the second examination are as follows: (1) Constitution (2) Criminal Law (3) Civil Law (4) Criminal Procedure Law (5) Civil Procedure Regulations (6) Various current laws and regulations regarding litigation (7) Court Organization Law (8) International Public Law (9) International Private Law. For the second to sixth subjects on the right, if the average score is failing, the scores of the remaining subjects, even if high, will not be accepted. Article 9: The subjects for the third examination are as follows: (1) Civil Law (2) Criminal Law (3) Commercial Law (4) Civil Procedure Regulations (5) Criminal Procedure Law. Article 10: A score of 70 out of 100 is required to pass each examination subject. Article 11: The total average examination score of 80 or more is considered Grade A, and 70 or more is considered Grade B. Article 13: Applicants for the Jiangsu County Trial Judge Examination must register at the Jiangsu County Trial Judge Examination Affairs Office within the registration period, pay a registration fee of 2 yuan, and obtain a resume and guarantee form. Article 14: The resume must be filled out by the applicant according to the prescribed format, with a recent 4-inch photograph attached. The guarantee form must be obtained from the guarantor and submitted with the supporting documents proving qualifications before the registration deadline. Article 15: The Chief Examiner shall submit the names and examination papers of those who pass the examination to the Minister of Judicial Administration and award the successful candidates with the Jiangsu

Page 10

County Trial Judge Examination Passing Certificate. The certificate fee is 4 yuan, and the stamp fee is 1 yuan. Article 16: Those who pass the examination may be sent by the President of the Jiangsu High Court to various local courts for practice. When there is a vacancy for a trial judge, they may be appointed at discretion. Registration period: November 24, 19, to January 6, 20. Examination date: January 19, 20.

Postal General Bureau Examines Postal Workers 144

Preliminary Exam of Three Thousand Five Hundred Candidates

Second Exam of Five Hundred Thirty-Three Candidates

Decision to Recruit Fifty Candidates

The Shanghai North Sichuan Road Postal General Bureau held an oral exam last Sunday to recruit postal workers. There were three thousand five hundred applicants. The Recruitment Committee evaluated the results of each subject and selected five hundred and thirty-three candidates who passed and were qualified for the second exam. Yesterday morning at 8:00 a.m., the written exam for the preliminary qualified candidates was held in the hall on the second floor of the bureau. All the candidates were present. The members of the Examination Committee, Hong Shengxiang, Zhang Shihan, Chen Lin, and more than thirty others, set the questions and strictly supervised the exam, so the examination site was in good order. The examination subjects were divided into six subjects: World Geography, Arithmetic, Chinese Language, Party Ideology, English, and General Knowledge. All subjects were completed on the same day, and the results will be announced in a month. It is heard that the Recruitment Committee of the bureau has decided to limit the number of people to be recruited to fifty. Once recruited, they will be assigned to various post offices in the city.

Meeting to Dredge Chunshen Pond 145

The Chunshen Pond waterway in western Shanghai extends from the Huangpu River to Songjiang County, spanning dozens of miles, and is an important waterway for the Shanghai and Songjiang counties. Recently, due to years of sedimentation, the relevant agencies and local people have discussed dredging it. Subsequently, the Municipal Port Authority and the Construction Bureaus of the two counties of Shanghai and Songjiang dispatched personnel to survey the accident site. At 2:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, a meeting was specially held at the Shanghai County Construction Bureau to discuss the project. Wu Wenhua and Sun Shengzeng, the directors of the Construction Bureaus of Shanghai and Songjiang counties, Dai Erjing, a technician from the Municipal Port Authority, Gong Maoxing, the chief of the Technology Section of the Shanghai Construction Bureau, and Gu Qi, Yang Songshi, Yang Xinzheng, and others from the Chunshen Pond Dredging Committee attended the meeting. After a long discussion, the following resolutions were immediately made: (1) Regarding the proposed width of the dredged Chunshen Pond waterway and how the bottom width and deepening should be stipulated, it was resolved to divide it into two types: township river and city river. (A) Township River: the width of the surface should be 20 meters and the width of the bottom should be 6 meters. (B) City River: the width of the surface should be 16 meters and the width of the bottom should be 6 meters. (C) The deepening should be 1.8 meters from the deepest point. (2) Regarding how to manage the dredging, it was resolved that the Shanghai Municipal Port Authority, the Shanghai County Construction Bureau, and the Songjiang County Construction Bureau should each send one person to supervise everything together with the Dredging Committee. The expenses will be provided by the committee. (3) Regarding whether the engineering budget should be compiled on a regular basis, it was decided that it should be compiled and submitted to the Dredging Committee before December 10. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 p.m.

Power Outage in the French Concession Last Night 148

At 7:15 p.m. last night, the lights in the French Concession suddenly went out completely from Zhengjia Muqiao Vegetable Market Street (i.e., Ningxing Street) to Dongxinqiao Street and the East and West Zilaishui Streets, and the area from Gongguan Road to the intersection of Avenue Edward VII was plunged into darkness. All the shops used candles and kerosene lamps instead. The French Electric and Gas Company then sent workers to repair it, which took about fifteen minutes before the lights were restored. After about ten minutes, the lights went out again. The police chief of the jurisdiction, fearing that bandits might take the opportunity to rob, sent Chinese and Western armed detectives to patrol the area until 8:20 p.m. when the lights were finally restored and shone brightly.

The Shanghai Cemetery Association of the Warehouse Industry has always been dedicated to searching for and burying exposed corpses and coffins. Intercepted a Native Opium Trafficker 151

They searched him and found a bag of native opium weighing 40 taels on Geng's side. They took the person and the goods to the station. Director Liu submitted a proposal for preliminary interrogation. Three People Found with Daggers and Ropes 153

Unsure of the Purpose

Pan Linsheng, the squad leader of the Tenth Team of the Shanghai South District Guard Corps, led his team members to patrol the area of Caoxi Road and Zhongshan Road at around 11:00 p.m. the night before last when he suddenly saw three people whispering in front of them. Squad Leader Pan, suspecting their suspicious behavior, went forward to search them and found a sharp dagger about eight inches long, two ropes (stained with blood), and two candles on the three people. He also found a small knife in his hat and took them all back to the team headquarters and sent them urgently to the Sixth District Second Precinct. Director Liu interrogated them strictly. Zhang Zhaoxiong, 26 years old, Lin Guanguan, 32 years old, and Chen Miaojin, 26 years old, all from Shanghai, lived in Qichang Warehouse in Pudong. Their statements were vague and they refused to tell the truth. Director Liu, believing that they were definitely not good people, sent the three people to the bureau for further investigation.

Yongan Company Introduces New Wool Flannel 154

The Yongan Company on Nanjing Road in the city has recently introduced a new type of domestically produced wool flannel that can replace leather goods and is the most economical product for keeping warm in winter. The price is 4 yuan per pound. According to the company, the wool is produced in the Tibetan border area of Dartse-do and Zhangjiakou. After the company has chemically treated it through skinning, selection, bleaching, disinfection, anti-corrosion, and other chemical processes, it is spun into flannel with a special elastic loosening machine. Therefore, the finished product is clean, white, light, and fluffy, and its warming effect is far beyond that of other cotton and wool products.

Her daughter's name is Hengzi, who is fourteen years old and currently living with her in a flat on Tokyo Road in Caozai Ferry. The woman seems to have a mental illness. The Sixth District was instructed to investigate her address, but no trace of the woman was found. The woman was wearing a torn black cotton-padded coat, torn black cloth lined trousers, black socks, and men's rubber rain boots. Habitual Offender Stealing Gold Lucky Charms 158

A-Kang Pleads Guilty to Robbery

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, in the small vegetable market in Nine Acres, a Wang woman was holding her child while buying vegetables when the robber Wang A-kang saw a gold lucky charm on the child's hand. He used scissors to cut the string and snatch it away. The Wang woman cried out for help, but in vain, and had to accept her bad luck. The robber then robbed a Jiang Zhang woman who was also buying vegetables and snatched a gold lucky charm from her child's hand before fleeing into the lane of Kaiming Hutong. Jiang Zhang cried out loudly for help, and Hou Zhaolin, the nineteenth watchman of the First Sub-station of the Second District, helped to capture and escort the robber to the station. After interrogation by Chief Qian, Wang A-kang confessed to the robbery. He was sentenced to be handed over to the Public Security Bureau for legal action.

Yesterday evening around 6:00 PM, a man resembling a worker, about forty years old, wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers, was walking near the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shilu when a Route 14 trolleybus sped by. He was unable to avoid it in time and was knocked to the ground, injuring his head. The eighteenth patrolman from the Lao Zha Police Station arrived and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. Assault After Failed Loan Request 160

Hu Guisheng, 27, who sets up a beef stall in the Ximo Road small vegetable market in West Shanghai and lives nearby at 61 Nanyang Road, was visited by his friend, Miao Fu, at 7:30 yesterday morning. Miao Fu said that his loan request was unsuccessful and left in a rage. A short while later, he gathered a group of hooligans and returned, luring Hu outside to a secluded spot. The hooligans suddenly attacked him with axes, striking him four times, twice in the shoulder, once in the back, and once in the back of the head. Bleeding profusely, Hu collapsed. Seeing the gravity of the situation, the assailants fled. The patrolmen No. 2626 from the Xin Zha Police Station arrived at the scene after hearing the alarm. Unable to catch the fleeing assailants, they hired a car to send the injured man to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Local News II

Letter from Xiao Xinan Overseas 162

Ms. Xiao Has Maintained Her Innocence Throughout

Upon Returning to the Country, She Can Request a Famous Doctor for Examination

Expressing Profound Gratitude for the Assistance of Fellow Chinese

Striving to Improve to Repay the Kindness of Compatriots

Original Text of the Apology Letter from the Java Company

Regarding the case of Ms. Xiao Xinan being insulted, this newspaper was the first to report on it, detailing the situation of compatriots from various places rising up to support her. Yesterday, this newspaper received a letter from Ms. Xiao from the Anbon Chinese Pei De School, describing everything in detail. We are now recording it for the readers' pleasure.

To the editor of Shenbao newspaper,

Your esteemed newspaper was the first to speak out for my injustice, causing compatriots across the country to rise up and help, for which I am deeply grateful. The situation of the incident has been reported in your newspaper, and the progress of the negotiations has also been recorded. Now, I will tell you what has not been mentioned. After the incident, Consul Tao negotiated with the shipowner on one hand and telegraphed Consul Wang in Makassar on the other to handle the matter. When the ship arrived in Makassar, I was taken to the Immigration Hall by the port police for questioning without any hindrance, which proves that I am not mentally ill (logically, those who are mentally ill would be sent to the hospital). After the questioning, I went to the consulate with my guarantor. An official came out to meet me and said that the ship had called to invite me to board the ship for negotiations. I then boarded the ship with my guarantor and his son. When we arrived at the pier, we were stopped by the police. I had to wait for a while before a Chinese crew member came down from the ship. I asked him to notify Consul Wang to come and take me on board. Soon after, Consul Wang and Consul Tao came down and said that the shipowner wanted to negotiate without publicizing it. I also agreed to their request, so when various groups and newspaper reporters came to inquire, I politely declined to answer. After several days, I only received a written apology and one person was punished. When the overseas Chinese in the South heard about it, they were even more indignant and informed me of the feelings of the overseas Chinese in the South and the power of the consulate to handle matters. I then publicized the negotiations to avoid future troubles for my compatriots. After the announcement, the Xiao Case Support Association was organized to unite various organizations to support Consul Wang. Schools and community groups in various places sent telegrams asking Consul Wang to negotiate to the end. Now I read in the Xinbao newspaper that the Java Batavia head office replied that they have agreed to dismiss the chief mate and issued a written apology to me, saying that the second mate had no evidence to confirm the charges and could not handle it. Recently, the Ambon government has received a document from a higher official asking me to investigate. I was interrogated at the government office yesterday and today with the principal of this school. I will continue to report on future situations. I respectfully wish you good health,

Xiao Xinan

P.S. I have enclosed a letter asking you to forward it.

Xiao Xinjing's Message 163

To the fathers, elders, brothers, sisters, aunts, and sisters of the nation:

This time I came south because I was introduced by the Education Bureau of the capital city of the motherland to start a business. I am eager to return home, and I especially cannot break faith with the authorities. I will not allow myself to do anything for any group that I do not agree with, but once I agree, I will never turn back. This is my nature, and I believe it is the spirit that one should have as a human being. Thinking back, I was displaced twice in Jiangbei during the war and lectured three times under artillery fire, but I never encountered any danger. This is known to my relatives and friends. Therefore, after falling into a lonely situation, there was no turning back, so I resolutely embarked on the journey. However, I had not been to the coast for eight years, and I had never seen a sea vessel. Before boarding the ship, I did not know anyone, and after boarding the ship, I lacked deep friendships. I encountered danger along the way and had no way to complain, so I could only find ways to protect myself and struggle with the thugs to avoid harm, first to comfort the heart of family education, and second to repay the cultivation of the motherland. Unexpectedly, the thugs took an inch and wanted a mile and even forced me to death. Fortunately, I relied on the long coat covering my head as a衬, wearing a long shirt and pants tied around my waist for protection, to avoid reaching their ultimate goal, leaving this innocence to comfort my compatriots. I am a woman who has not been sexually assaulted. In the future, when I return to my country, I can ask a famous doctor to examine me to prove it. After the pain in my heart, this is the only thing that can comfort my family and relatives. If I continue to endure this in the end, I am afraid that I will cause trouble for my compatriots, and I also believe that there is no guilt in my heart, so I do not need to be afraid to speak. I am willing to sacrifice everything to announce the truth to encourage people. Recently, I read in the newspaper that compatriots in the motherland heard the news and rose up to help me, which is very fortunate. Yesterday, I read in the Xinbao newspaper that the Java Batavia head office replied that the chief mate had agreed to be dismissed and issued a written apology to me, saying that the second mate had no evidence to confirm the charges and could not handle it. I am a person who studies education. Now that modern science is flourishing, I sincerely hope to use psychological experiments to clarify the truth about their actions that are upside down and bury their conscience, and negotiate to the end. I deeply hope that all sectors of the motherland will help me find a world-renowned hypnotist and hand over these two thugs to the Java Company for experiments. Recently, I read an advertisement in the Shenbao newspaper column that the hypnosis of the China Spiritual Research Association on Xihaining Road, Beisichuan Road, Shanghai can explore the right and wrong of crimes effectively. I also hope that compatriots who care about my case will inquire about it. In the unlikely event that the negotiations can be achieved, I will return my carefree life from this sad remaining life, work hard to fulfill my responsibilities, save a little money, and then go to various countries to investigate education, hoping to return to my country in the future to make a small contribution to repay the kindness of compatriots across the country. I only wish that things would be as I hope, but the world is full of vicissitudes and human affairs are unpredictable, which is worrying. And I ask my relatives and friends not to be concerned about my personal misfortune. From now on, work hard for the country to increase its strength and reduce internal strife and external insults. This is what I hope. I will wait for the sadness to subside a little and record in the newspaper the experiences and feelings of this trip, the common sense of the waterway experienced by a woman alone, and the attitude to respond to danger and the things to prepare for danger, so as to avoid compatriots from following in my footsteps. As I write, I am sad and cannot express all my feelings.

After Jiang Weiqiao Was Kidnapped

The Process of Contacting the Bandits 164

The Bandits Sent Three Letters

Arranging Negotiations in a Hotel

The Victim Went as Agreed

But There Was No News

Jiang Weiqiao, the owner of the Jiang Xiangxing Slaughterhouse Company on Xijiaotong Road, Zhabei, was kidnapped on the evening of the 23rd of last month at 6:30 PM when he boarded his own cargo truck to go to the distribution point on Kangnuot Road. Details have been recorded in this newspaper. A month has passed and he is still in danger. Yesterday, this newspaper reporter happened to meet a close relative of Jiang's at a banquet, who described the process of contacting the bandits in detail. Now, I will record what the relative said.

The First Letter The relative said (the following is all the relative's words): After Jiang was kidnapped on the 23rd of last month, the whole family was extremely anxious, especially Jiang's brother, Weibin (also known as Taikang). For almost ten days, the bandits had no response and there was no news. It was not until the 29th that a letter came directly to Jiang Weibin. The envelope was addressed to "Mr. Jiang Taikang, 16 Fengtian Road, American Concession, Shanghai." It was signed "Yue Jian." Inside, in addition to a piece of paper written by the bandits, there was also a ransom note in the victim's handwriting. The letter stated that the victim was chained in the bandit's den, suffering from dysentery, and urged his brother to quickly prepare the full ransom of 300,000 yuan to redeem him.

Demanding 300,000 Yuan The bandit's letter stated: "Your brother (referring to the victim) is being treated very well here, but because there are many colleagues in our department and the economy is exhausted, we plan to temporarily borrow 300,000 yuan from you to meet our urgent needs." It also stated: "If you sincerely want to negotiate, please publish the advertisement on the first page of Shenbao according to the following draft, with the number representing 10,000. For example, if you agree to 300,000 yuan, then publish 300 yuan." Therefore, on the 1st of this month, a missing person advertisement was found in the second advertisement of this newspaper. The original manuscript is recorded below: "Missing Person Yesterday, a black leather bag was lost on the way, containing several important documents and a round seal with the篆文character Yue Xiang. If anyone finds it, please send it to (Room 84, Jue Lu Hotel). A reward of 15 yuan will be paid immediately, and we will never go back on our word. Yue Xiang"

Second Warning After the victim's brother, Jiang Taikang, published the advertisement as ordered, the so-called reward of 15 yuan meant agreeing to a price of 150,000 yuan. Two days later, the bandits sent another letter stating: "After reading the report, we know that the agreed price is too different and there is no possibility of negotiation. Your Excellency (referring to Weibin) must not be sincere. We are sending another letter as a warning, hoping that you will reconsider and publish the lowest price as a reply to make a final decision." After Taikang received the letter, he published another advertisement asking the bandits to arrange a date and time to contact him directly at Jiang's residence at 16 Fengtian Road.

No News From Then On After Taikang published the advertisement for the second time, another week passed and the bandits sent a third letter stating: "Since you want to negotiate face-to-face, please open a room with the largest telephone at the New World Hotel on Nanjing Road tomorrow. The name on the passenger list at the door must be Hu. Someone will come to contact you then." The letter also included a note in the victim's handwriting, generally asking his brother to quickly find a way to rescue him. Jiang's family prepared as instructed, but no one came that night. Since then, there has been no news.

Father Kills Daughter Out of Hatred 165

The Father Gave All He Had to Marry Off His Daughter

The Daughter Refused to Help Her Father at All

Filled with Extreme Hatred, He Tried to Kill Her with a Knife

Wu Maomao, a villager in Zhoujiaqiao in West Shanghai, makes a living growing flowers. He had a daughter, Wu Shi, who married Gao Shidao, the son of Gao Shaoqing, who lives in Gaojiahang, south of Zhoujiaqiao, two years ago. Wu Maomao wanted to save face, so the dowry was especially rich, so that he spent all his savings and even mortgaged the base land for money. This is the harm of vanity. Wu had no rice to cook, so last year he and a friend ran a flower shed to make a living. Wu complained to his daughter, asking her to speak to her parents-in-law and husband to borrow one or two hundred yuan as capital, and he would repay them with interest. If not, then twenty or thirty yuan would also be fine to start a small business. He expected a reply in about a week, but the daughter was indifferent and did not reply. Wu went to inquire and was ridiculed by Gao Shaoqing and others, which was extremely embarrassing. He was very resentful in his heart. This year, because of various unsatisfactory things, the flower shed run by his friend was very prosperous. Wu thought that if his daughter had a little human heart and helped him, he would not be as prosperous as others and his own life would be so desolate. He hated her so much that he had the idea of killing her. Yesterday morning, he knew that his daughter would definitely go to the yarn factory to work, so he waited on the road with a sharp knife. When his daughter passed by, he grabbed her and stabbed her hard in the ribs. The daughter cried out for help. Gao and others rushed out and grabbed Wu, snatching the knife, but the daughter had already been stabbed in the waist, bleeding all over her body, and was seriously injured. They then ordered the police to come and arrest Wu at the Sixth District Police Station, and sent the injured person to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. In the afternoon, the district transferred the two parties to the local court for interrogation.

American Engineer Stabs English Constable 166

Defendant Du Ke Sentenced to Imprisonment and Fine

The Zi Lin Bao reported that Du Ke, the deck engineer of the American ship Ai Wuwa, was drunk and disorderly in a bar on Broadway last Sunday, stabbing the English constable Qin Jinsheng. The case was reopened in the American consulate on Saturday. Qin Jinsheng was first called to testify that he went to the bar for a drink last Sunday morning and met his friend Mo Le. While they were standing and talking, the defendant, who was already drunk, joined in with slanderous words. He pushed him aside, and the defendant stood between the two of them again and spoke rudely. He then lightly struck his nose and continued to talk to Mo Le as before. Not long after, Mo Le was suddenly punched in the back of the head, and he also felt that he had been hit from behind. He immediately fell to the ground, and Mo Le saw blood on his clothes and realized that he had been stabbed and injured. He was sent to the hospital, and the defendant had already disappeared. After describing the events, he presented the bloody clothes as evidence. Mo Le was then called to testify and gave the same account. The defendant Du Ke also admitted to being drunk and disorderly, but said that he could not remember the situation at the time. Finally, the prosecutor argued that although there was no concrete evidence to prove who stabbed Qin Jinsheng, all the witnesses pointed to the defendant. The judge then sentenced Du Ke to 60 days in prison and fined him $100.

Trolley Derails at Stealing Chicken Bridge 167

Traffic Blocked for Twenty Minutes

Yesterday evening at 6:35 PM, a Route 5 trolleybus traveling from the West Gate to the North Railway Station derailed its rear carriage when it reached the Stealing Chicken Bridge station on North Zhejiang Road. The wheels rolled on the road, scattering sparks. The passengers on the carriage were panicked. The driver quickly stopped the bus, and the passengers jumped off one after another. They then tried to drag it back onto the track, but half of the wheel suddenly fell into the adjacent track, making it even more difficult. As a result, more than twenty trolleybuses traveling to and from Nanjing Road to the Garbage Bridge were unable to move forward. For a time, the onlookers gathered and the traffic was blocked. After twenty minutes, the carriage was driven back onto its original track, and the buses gradually moved and returned to their original state.

Xin Case Support Association Hosts Press 172

Last night at six o'clock, the Xin Dingxiang Tragedy Support Association hosted news reporters from various newspapers and news agencies in this port at the Fuxing Garden on Simalu (Four Horse Road). During the event, Chairman Cheng Zhiliang, Ni Yaoxian, Cai Xiaohe, and Yang Yiqing, among others, reported on the details of the tragedy, stating that the Xin case had occurred several days ago, and the French imperialists had shown no sincerity in resolving it. This demonstrates their disregard for China. For the sake of national survival and to protect national sovereignty, Chinese people should vow to fight for the Xin case. It is hoped that the press will advocate for humanity and justice, widely publish the French's reliance on strength and their brutal actions, so that people around the world can know the true face of the French. Subsequently, Guan Jiu'an, a reporter from the Republican Daily, was publicly elected by the press to deliver a response. The event concluded at nine o'clock.

The Seven Major Labor Unions, including the local Postal Workers' Union, the Commercial Workers' Union, the Chinese Electrical Workers' Union, the China Merchants Bureau Workers' Union, the Press Workers' Union, and the British-American Tobacco Factory Workers' Union, issued a declaration yesterday regarding the Xin Dingxiang Tragedy. The text is recorded as follows for the public to see: Fellow compatriots across the country, French imperialists, with their gunboat policy, run rampant in our country, treating us as a second-class colony. Our entire nation is like meat on a chopping board. Thinking of this, we are filled with pain and resentment. This time, a French warship, the "Waldeck-Rousseau," had a sailor who, when hailing a sampan to return to the ship, was asked by the sampan operator, Xin Dingxiang, to pay the ferry fare. Unexpectedly, the sailor brutally assaulted Xin and pushed him into the river, causing him to drown. When the news spread, the whole country was indignant. After serious negotiations by the Tragedy Support Association, the French Consul-General in Shanghai, Gan Gelin, replied to the Municipal Government, stating in the document that the murderer had been severely punished by the naval authorities. The wording was vague, and it was just empty words to shirk responsibility. The French authorities' lack of sincerity in resolving the matter is already clear. French imperialists have invaded our sovereignty, insulted our national integrity, and slaughtered our people. They have been doing this for a long time and it has only gotten worse. Our union believes that unless we rely on the strength of the government and the support of the people to engage in serious and uncompromising negotiations with the French authorities, we will not be able to deter the arrogance of the French imperialists. In addition to the Support Association continuing to petition the government to protest seriously, we must be sure to achieve the goal of punishing the murderer according to the law, paying compensation and pensions, and guaranteeing that similar incidents will not happen again in the future. In addition to our union providing support, we also hope that the entire nation will unite and rise up together to carry out the movement to recover concessions, abolish consular jurisdiction, withdraw the naval and land forces of all countries stationed in China, and abolish all unequal treaties. This is our declaration.

Jiang Chun Kai Failed to Appear in Court

Ma Wenlin's Power is Extremely Strong

The case was continued by Judge Feng the day before yesterday. The plaintiff, Jiang Chunkai, did not appear in court. Therefore, he could not appear in court today. He requested that a letter be sent to the Public Security Bureau to transfer Jiang. The defendant, Ma Wenlin, has extremely strong power, with over a thousand followers. The police searched his home and found Ma's business card, with the meeting time engraved on the back. This is evident and the card was submitted as evidence. Subsequently, witnesses Wang Fanshi, Zhao Sunshi, and others separately testified that Ma and Yu went to Jiang's residence that day, accusing Jiang of being a communist party member, intending to extort money, and assaulting Zhao Sunshi, injuring her. Ma denied that the business card was engraved by him. As for his actions of extorting money from Jiang that day, his testimony was similar to the previous one, constantly shirking responsibility. Yu Renbiao testified that he was forced to go by Ma. Judge Feng ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody and a letter to be sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to inquire about the reason for Jiang Chunkai's detention. The case was adjourned for review.

Lawsuit to Terminate a Marriage Engagement 178

Underage

Wait Until Next Year to Sue Again

Yang Shouzeng, a partner in Yuyuan Qianzhuang, was engaged to Feng Jiafen by his father, Yang Cangsheng. At the time, both Yang and Feng were only fourteen years old. Now, they are both nearing adulthood. Feng, because her parents did not seek her consent at the time of the engagement and she is not yet formally married, believes that she can still remedy the situation. She came to Shanghai from her original home in Cixi, temporarily residing at her uncle's house at No. 412, Xintangjia Lane, to negotiate the termination of the engagement. However, Yang Shouzeng strongly opposed it. Feng then sued in the Special District Court, requesting that the engagement be terminated based on the principle of freedom of marriage. Judge Ying Shiting opened the court the day before yesterday and summoned the defendant, Yang Shouzeng, who did not appear. The plaintiff, Feng Jiafen, then stated:

Page 12

I am now twenty years old. This engagement was arranged by my parents, and I knew nothing about it beforehand. Therefore, I am unwilling to marry him, so I filed a lawsuit. Judge Ying then inquired when she was born, since she claimed to be twenty years old. Feng replied that her birthday was May 11th. The defendant's lawyer then stated that the civil law stipulates that one must be twenty years old to be considered an adult, and only adults have the capacity for legal action. Otherwise, legal actions must be represented by a legal guardian. The plaintiff's age is actually only nineteen, and she does not have the right to sue according to the law. Judge Ying agreed that the defendant's lawyer's statement was reasonable and advised the plaintiff: You are not yet of legal age. If you want to sue, you must be represented by a parent. However, the engagement you are requesting to revoke was permitted and established by your parents, so they will not agree to revoke it. In order to protect your legal interests, you should withdraw the case for now and file a lawsuit in this court again on May 12th of next year, when you turn twenty. Feng Jiafen was deeply grateful for the judge's kindness in considering both law and reason and authorized her lawyer to withdraw the lawsuit in court.

Master Ordered to Pay Compensation of 100 Silver Dollars

Ding Shijun from Anhui previously hired a lawyer to represent him in the French court, claiming that the plaintiff's mother had been working in the defendant Zhou Mingji's house as a maid and was accused by a fellow maid, A Cai, of stealing items, causing her to commit suicide out of anger. Many Twists and Turns in the Kidnapping of a Country Girl 181

Riya Bank Is Not a Pharmacy

Kidnapped to Pudong, Case Cracked by Police

Li Yuebao, a 14-year-old girl from Jiading, had a pretty face and loved to be fashionable. She was very close to Zhang Zhao, a neighboring woman. Recently, Zhang Zhao suddenly became blind and planned to come to Shanghai with her son, Zhang Guohua, for medical treatment. Li Yuebao also planned to come to Shanghai to play and serve her. With the consent of Yuebao's parents, they came to Shanghai and stayed at the Hui'an Hotel on Zhejiang Road. They had a lot of fun treating the illness and playing. Unexpectedly, Li Koutu, a man from Tongzhou who had worked as a craftsman in Jiading Hongmu, encountered Zhang Guohua and asked him why he had come to Shanghai. Zhang replied that he was treating his mother's illness. Li Koutu then took Qu Longchang, also from Tongzhou who had also worked in Jiading Hongmu, to the hotel and invited Zhang Guohua and others to play together. Li Yuebao wanted to return home because a neighbor had asked her to buy headache medicine. She begged Zhang Guohua to take her to a pharmacy. So they went together. Because the country people were unfamiliar with the way, Qu Longchang pointed to Riya Bank as a pharmacy. Because there were many vehicles, Qu Longchang and Li Yuebao stood at the north end of the bank waiting for Zhang Guohua to go south alone. When Zhang reached the bank, he inquired and found that it was a bank, not a pharmacy. He had to turn back, but he did not see Li Yuebao and Qu Longchang. He was quite shocked and searched everywhere without success. He had to return to the residence and tell Zhang Zhao. Zhang Zhao was planning to ask someone to report to the police and search for them when Qu Longchang suddenly came to the door. Zhang asked where Li Yuebao was. Qu replied that she was now in Pudong. If he wanted to get her back, he would have to pay 150 silver dollars. Zhang replied, "Where would I get so much money?" Qu actually punched him. Then, he left angrily and went to a friend named He at Sanmaoge Bridge. Zhang immediately tracked him down with his mother. Zhang Zhao grabbed Qu Longchang and refused to let go, shouting for the French police to bring the group to the police station. According to Qu Longchang's confession, he had kidnapped Li Yuebao to Pudong, but he was questioned by a patrolman from the Third District, and Li was detained while he escaped. The French police determined that the incident occurred in the Chinese Concession and transferred the defendant to the Second District First Section yesterday afternoon at about 4:00 PM. Chief Qian interrogated Qu Longchang and determined that he had committed the act of kidnapping and selling a good family's daughter. He was sentenced to be transferred to the Public Security Bureau for legal action.

Woman Dies by Poisoning 185

Wu Zhaogan from Tengxian County, Shandong, 55 years old, was a worker in the arsenal and lived at No. 2727, Longhua Road, behind the Weibaotuan in Jijiawan. A fellow villager named Duan opened a small cigarette and paper shop there. Recently, Duan and Wu had disagreements and often slandered each other. Yesterday, Wu went to question Duan, and there was a big conflict. Wu broke all the items on the counter in Duan's shop and returned home angrily. The anger had not subsided, and at the same time, he felt that breaking other people's property would not end well if the police were reported. The feelings of anger and fear were intertwined, so he felt that it was better to commit suicide. He secretly bought opium at a nearby cigarette shop and swallowed it. By the time the poison took effect, no one knew, and his husband came home from work and found out, but it was too late to save him. He was greatly saddened and twisted Duan to the local police station and sent him to the Sixth District Third Section for submission to the Public Security Bureau. In addition, the local guarantor Xu Jinliang reported to the local court for an autopsy. Zhao, the prosecutor, and others came to the scene to examine the body and determined that it was suicide by swallowing opium. He ordered the relatives to collect the body and wait for the Public Security Bureau to resolve the case.

Lost Boy Sent to Bureau for Custody 187

Jiangbei Accent

Yesterday afternoon at 8:00 PM, a lost boy about seven or eight years old was crying on the side of Hudong Road in West Shanghai. He was brought back to the Sixth District Second Section by patrol officer Shi Wenjin. He was asked his name and address, but he did not know much. He seemed to have a Jiangbei accent. He was wearing a black hat, a printed cloth shirt, black cloth pants, patterned socks, and black shoes. Because no one claimed him, he was sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for custody, waiting for his family to claim him.

Zhang Ye'er's Family's Carelessness 188

No. 7, Yongan Lane, Guangxi Road, the residence of famous comedian Zhang Ye'er, suddenly caught fire yesterday morning at 8:45 AM. The fire pierced the roof.

The fierce flames spread and burned down the neighboring house at No. 8. The fire brigade rushed to the scene to put out the fire, and it was quickly extinguished. A total of two houses were destroyed.

Robberies Also Recorded 189

Yesterday morning at 1:00 AM, four thugs came to No. 315, Shanxi Road, Public Concession. Two of them were holding pistols and threatened the victim, robbing him of clothes and jewelry estimated to be worth 170 silver dollars. The victim reported the incident to the Hongkou Police Station, requesting an investigation.

Yesterday morning at around 4:30 AM, a Mr. Jia, riding in a rickshaw, was robbed while traveling on Xinzha Road. A thug emerged from the alley, and two of them, carrying axes and one holding a pistol, blocked the road and searched him. Unfortunately, there was nothing of value in his pockets, only a few copper coins. The clothes he was wearing were also not worth much, causing the robbers to be disappointed. They injured him in two places with an axe. The robbers then escaped empty-handed.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather was clear and cold, with strong northwest to northeast winds along the coast of the country. There would be snow on the coast of Shandong and in northern Korea. The highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 56.7 degrees, and the lowest was 46.8 degrees.
